16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"For Warmth: Thich Nhat Hanh’s Poetic Antidote to Anger","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75772","description":"<h3>How to keep your soul from leaving you.</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Call-Me-True-Names-Collected/dp/1952692261/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?fit=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"For Warmth: Thich Nhat Hanh&#8217;s Poetic Antidote to Anger\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?resize=320%2C480&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?resize=600%2C900&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?resize=240%2C360&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/callmebymytruenames_thichnhathanh.jpg?resize=1024%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1024w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“The main thing is this &#8212; when you get up in the morning you must take your heart in your two hands,&#8221; the poet and storyteller turned activist Grace Paley&#8217;s father told her in what remains <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/09/03/grace-paley-aging/\">the finest advice on growing older</a>. &#8220;You must do this every morning.”</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, the Vietnamese Zen monk and peace activist turned poet <strong>Thich Nhat Hanh</strong> (October 11, 1926&#8211;January 22, 2022), just a few years younger than Paley, was channeling a kindred sentiment into one of his poems as he watched the world come undone by the oldest ugliness in the bosom of the human animal, in a war breaking countless hearts and robbing countless lives of the gift of growing older.</p>\n<p>Upon learning that the city of Ben Tre had been bombed and hearing an American officer declare, in his recollection, &#8220;that he had to destroy the town in order to save the town,&#8221; Thich Nhat Hanh saw war clearly for what it is &#8212; a pinnacle of the anger with which we humans so often cover up our loneliness, the loneliness which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2016/12/20/hannah-arendt-origins-of-totalitarianism-loneliness-isolation/\">tyrants so often use to flare up terror</a>.  </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75703\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=680%2C1009&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1009\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75703\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=320%2C475&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=600%2C890&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=240%2C356&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=768%2C1139&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/thichnhathanh_plumvillage.jpg?resize=1036%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1036w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Thich Nhat Hanh. (Photograph courtesy of <a href=\"https://plumvillage.org/about/thich-nhat-hanh/biography\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Plum Village</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>A salve, a self-consolation, a spare and powerful spell against anger &#8212; the most fundamental and fundamentalist war against ourselves &#8212; the poem calls to mind poet May Sarton&#8217;s exquisite conception of anger as <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2016/11/04/may-sarton-anger/\">&#8220;a huge creative urge gone into reverse.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<p>Published decades later in <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Call-Me-True-Names-Collected/dp/1952692261/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Call Me by My True Names: The Collected Poems of Thich Nhat Hanh</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/call-me-by-my-true-names-the-collected-poems-of-thich-nhat/oclc/1196202278&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>), as the world was coming undone anew in the self-redundantly named &#8220;war on terror,&#8221; it is read here by Thich Nhat Hanh himself in its original Vietnamese, then by Krista Tippett in English, as part of their altogether <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/programs/remembering-thich-nhat-hanh-brother-thay/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">shimmering 2002 conversation</a> about the practice of mindfulness and compassion at the heart of our humanity:</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"&#34;For Warmth&#34; by Thich Nhat Hanh by brainpicker\" width=\"680\" height=\"400\" scrolling=\"no\" frameborder=\"no\" src=\"https://w.soundcloud.com/player/?visual=true&#038;url=https%3A%2F%2Fapi.soundcloud.com%2Ftracks%2F1207926772&#038;show_artwork=true&#038;maxheight=1000&#038;maxwidth=680\"></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>FOR WARMTH</strong><br />\n<em>by Thich Nhat Hanh</em></p>\n<p>I hold my face between my hands.<br />\nNo, I am not crying.<br />\nI hold my face between my hands<br />\nto keep my loneliness warm &#8212;<br />\ntwo hands protecting,<br />\ntwo hands nourishing,<br />\ntwo hands to prevent<br />\nmy soul from leaving me<br />\nin anger.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In his <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/programs/remembering-thich-nhat-hanh-brother-thay/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>On Being</em> conversation</a> with Krista, Thich Nhat Hanh unpeels the poetic abstraction to reflect on the underlying practice the verse speaks to &#8212; mindfulness (which in 2002 was far from a mainstream notion in the West) as a practical antidote to anger:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The individual has to wake up to the fact that violence cannot end violence; that only understanding and compassion can neutralize violence, because with the practice of loving speech and compassionate listening we can begin to understand people and help people to remove the wrong perceptions in them, because these wrong perceptions are at the foundation of their anger, their fear, their violence, their hate.</p>\n<p>[&#8230;]</p>\n<p>We have to remain human in order to be able to understand and to be compassionate. You have the right to be angry, but you don’t have the right not to practice in order to transform your anger&#8230; When you notice that anger is coming up in you, you have to practice mindful breathing in order to generate the energy of mindfulness, in order to recognize your anger and embrace it tenderly so that you can bring relief into you and not to act and to say things&#8230; that can be destructive. And doing so, you can look deeply into the nature of your anger and know where it has come from.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement with Ursula K. Le Guin on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2017/12/05/ursula-k-le-guin-no-time-to-spare-anger/\">anger and its antidote</a>, then revisit Thich Hhat Hanh on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/10/thich-nhat-hanh-listening-love/\">the art of deep listening</a>, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/12/01/thich-nhat-hanh-fear-love/\">the four Buddhist mantras for turning fear into love</a>, and his lovely youthful account of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/01/23/thich-nhat-hanh-fragrant-palm-leaves/\">the library epiphany in which he lost his self and found himself</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. See the rest <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/the-universe-in-verse/\">here</a>.</em></p>\n<h5>THE ANIMATED UNIVERSE IN VERSE: CHAPTER FIVE</h5>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/animations.jpg?w=532&#038;ssl=1\" /></a>Whenever I am down, I think of the gladiolus.</p>\n<p>Whenever I ache with self-referential humanity &#8212; that evolutionary miracle of complex consciousness that endows us with the capacity for reflection and rumination at the root of all sorrow &#8212; I think of the gladiolus and its primal scream of color and its <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">two-hundred-million-year triumph</a>, governed by insentient forces stretching back to the Big Bang that bloomed a something out of the unimaginable nothingness.</p>\n<p>I think of the gladiolus with its mohawk of blossoms &#8212; one-sided, bisexual, belonging to nature&#8217;s nonbinary citizenry: the <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/07/02/perfect-flowers-emily-dickison/\">&#8220;perfect flowers&#8221;</a> &#8212; most of its 300 known species native to Africa, to which we too are native. A fierce beauty named after the Latin word for <em>sword</em>, known sometimes as &#8220;sword lily,&#8221; linking it to the flower for which my mother was named. A blade of blossoms pollinated by tiny wasps and long-tongued bees and hawk-moths, and then by self-conscious sapiens with opposable thumbs &#8212; a chainlink of humans holding hands across the epochs from Mendel to the young Puerto Rican woman at the Manhattan flower market, those generations of horticulturalists who hybridized and cultivated the small iridescent blossoms of the wild flower to make the towering blooms of solid red and white and yellow in my Bulgarian grandmother&#8217;s garden, on my Bulgarian grandfather&#8217;s coffin. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76177\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/gladiolus-by-sydenham-teast-edwards-1790-benefitting-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=680%2C1084&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"1084\" class=\"size-full wp-image-76177\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=320%2C510&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=600%2C957&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=240%2C383&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=768%2C1224&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/gladiolus_williamcurtis_1790.jpg?resize=964%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 964w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Gladiolus by Sydenham Teast Edwards from William Curtis&#8217;s <em>Botanical Magazine</em>, 1790. (Available as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/gladiolus-by-sydenham-teast-edwards-1790-benefitting-the-nature-conservancy_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">print</a> and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?sort=new?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, benefitting The Nature Conservancy.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>I think of the gladiolus, with which we share 98% of our DNA &#8212; that delicate arrangement of atoms forged long ago when all of them, yours and mine and the sword lily&#8217;s, banged into being 13.8 billion years ago from a single source, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\">no larger than the dot levitating over the small <em>i</em>, the I lowered from the pedestal of ego</a>.</p>\n<p>The young poet <a href=\"https://www.marissa-davis.com/about\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Marissa Davis</a> celebrates the atomic spirituality in this chainlink of kinship between us and everything alive in <strong>&#8220;Singularity (after Marie Howe)&#8221;</strong> &#8212; a poem inspired by <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/04/23/singularity-marie-howe-animated/\">&#8220;Singularity (after Stephen Hawking),&#8221;</a> which the gifted and golden-souled Marie Howe composed for and <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/05/22/singularity-marie-howe-stephen-hawking/\">premiered at</a> the second annual <em>Universe in Verse</em> in 2018, commemorating the recently stardust-surrendered scientist who revolutionized our understanding of the universe by illuminating what happens to a dying star as it collapses to form a singularity &#8212; the tiny point of zero radius, infinite density, and infinite curvature of spacetime at the bottom of a black hole, kindred to the Big Bang singularity at the bottom of the Beginning &#8212; that original seed from which the universe bloomed. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=680%2C372&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"372\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-76186\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?w=1913&#38;ssl=1 1913w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=320%2C175&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=600%2C328&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=240%2C131&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=768%2C420&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?resize=1536%2C840&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lottiekingslake.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>Marie&#8217;s &#8220;Singularity&#8221; &#8212; which was transformed into a breathtaking <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/04/23/singularity-marie-howe-animated/\">animated film</a> for the lockdown livestream of the 2020 show, a film that inspired this experimental literary-animated &#8220;season&#8221; of <em>The Universe in Verse</em> in the interlude between live gatherings &#8212; radiated across our Pale Blue Dot, eventually reaching Marissa to spark her own &#8220;Singularity&#8221; &#8212; an exquisite ode to our primeval bond with one another and the rest of nature. </p>\n<p>For this fifth installment in the interlude series, in an homage to the intergenerational chainlink of inspiration from which all art is born, here is Marissa&#8217;s &#8220;Singularity&#8221; animated into vibrant aliveness by English artist <a href=\"https://lottiekingslake.co.uk\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lottie Kingslake</a> and set to song by the cosmic life-force that is <a href=\"https://www.printmag.com/podcasts/2021/design-matters-toshi-reagon/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Toshi Reagon</a>.</p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Universe in Verse | Part 5: Singularity\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/679582022?h=5828d8417d&#38;dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/thefragilespecies_lewisthomas.jpg?resize=600%2C904&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/thefragilespecies_lewisthomas.jpg?resize=240%2C362&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/thefragilespecies_lewisthomas.jpg?resize=768%2C1157&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>When Earth first erupted with color, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">flowers took over so suddenly and completely</a> that, two hundred million years later, the baffled Darwin called this blooming conquest an &#8220;abominable mystery.&#8221; </p>\n<p>When earthlings first realized that our Milky Way is not the cosmic whole but one galactic particle of the whole &#8212; one of unfathomably many galaxies, each abloom with billions of stars orbited by other worlds &#8212; the universe suddenly appeared <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/11/universe-in-verse-animated-hubble/\">&#8220;so brutal and alive it seemed to comprehend us back.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<p>When it became clear that a mysterious substance is holding each galaxy together, keeping each world&#8217;s orbit a perfect corolla around the stigma of its star, we gave that substance a name befitting an abominable mystery: dark matter. </p>\n<p>Along the way, we &#8212; thinking, feeling, meaning-hungry creatures &#8212; kept trying to make beauty of the truths we found, composing <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">poems about flowers</a> and <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/24/dark-matter/\">poems about dark matter</a> as we composed our equations and our theories.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76132\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/24/dark-matter/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=680%2C441&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"441\" class=\"size-full wp-image-76132\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?w=2131&#38;ssl=1 2131w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=320%2C208&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=600%2C389&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=240%2C156&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=768%2C498&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=1536%2C996&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=2048%2C1328&#38;ssl=1 2048w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Ohara Hale for <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/24/dark-matter/\">&#8220;Let There Always be Light (Searching for Dark Matter)&#8221;</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Reality&#8217;s ability to continually baffle us with what we don&#8217;t yet know, and our willingness to continually plumb the unknown for new truth and beauty, even as it baffles and terrifies us, is the loveliest thing about being alive. Being alive together, as members of this boundlessly inquisitive and imaginative species, is the loveliest thing about being human.</p>\n<p>That is what <strong>Lewis Thomas</strong> (November 25, 1913&#8211;December 3, 1993) &#8212; a scientist, poet, and perhaps <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/lewis-thomas/\">my favorite</a> writer about the native poetics of reality &#8212; explores throughout his altogether exquisite final essay collection, <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Fragile-Species-Lewis-Thomas/dp/0684843021/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Fragile Species</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/fragile-species/oclc/264933186&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76133\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lewisthomas_galaxy.jpg?resize=595%2C737&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"595\" height=\"737\" class=\"size-full wp-image-76133\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lewisthomas_galaxy.jpg?w=595&#38;ssl=1 595w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lewisthomas_galaxy.jpg?resize=320%2C396&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lewisthomas_galaxy.jpg?resize=240%2C297&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 595px) 100vw, 595px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">A galactic Lewis Thomas</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the opening essay, originally delivered as a talk in 1987 for the fiftieth reunion of his Harvard Medical School class, Thomas reflects on the splendid bafflements of science since he and his classmates parted ways in the prime of their lives half a century earlier. With his signature winking genius, he writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I cannot count the number of new items of ignorance I&#8217;ve picked up in fifty years; the list is simply too long. Instead, I have prepared another kind of list, shorter, more personally humbling, of some things I think I might have been learning more about if I hadn&#8217;t been so puzzled all those years by medicine itself. There are matters that I assume most other people my age comprehend nicely, and I never got round to studying.</p>\n<p>The Federal Reserve System is at the top of my list. I&#8217;ve never known what it was or what it did or how it did it, and what is more I don&#8217;t want to be told. The same goes for the stock market, and for the bond market, and the word processor (one of which I actually possess and am baffled by), and the internal combustion engine, and the universe, black holes, galactic mirrors, those other universes, and space-time. Most of all, space-time. I cannot get ahold of it.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76134\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/11/universe-in-verse-animated-hubble/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=680%2C359&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"359\" class=\"size-full wp-image-76134\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?w=2560&#38;ssl=1 2560w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=320%2C169&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=600%2C316&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=240%2C127&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=768%2C405&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=1536%2C810&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=2048%2C1080&#38;ssl=1 2048w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Daniel Bruson for <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/11/universe-in-verse-animated-hubble/\">&#8220;My God, It&#8217;s Full of Stars&#8221;</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>With so fetching a wink, Thomas turns to the real object of his meditation: our native inability to comprehend how the same processes that begot these remote abstractions also begot the fleshy, feeling concreteness of us. There is something incredibly lovely about Thomas&#8217;s warm humor &#8212; here is man of extraordinary intellect, scientific erudition, and uncommon human sensitivity, inviting the rest of us, far more ordinary and modestly lettered, to join him in his gladsome bafflement at the seeming miracle of life:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I even have troubles of my own with evolutionary biology. Not first principles, mind you, not the big picture, mostly just the details. I understand about randomness and chance, and election, and adaptation, and all that, and I now know better than to talk, ever, about progress in evolution, never mind purpose. My problems come when I think about the earliest form of known life, those indisputable bacterial cells in rocks 3.7 billion years old, our Ur-grandparents for sure, then nothing but bacteria for the next two and one-half billion years, and now the chestnut tree in my backyard, my Abyssinian cat Jeoffry, the almost-but-not-quite free-living microbes living in all our cells disguised as mitochondria, and, just by the way, our marvelous, still-immature, dangerous selves, brainy enough to menace all nature unless distracted by music.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Leaning on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/08/11/lewis-thomas-notes-on-punctuation/\">his training as an etymologist</a> &#8212; that is, an evolutionary biologist for the living organism of language &#8212; Thomas adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We need a better word than chance, even pure chance, or that succession of events, while still evading any notion of progress. But to go all the way from a clone of archaebacteria, in just 3.7 billion years, to the B-Minor Mass and the Late Quartets, deserves a better technical term for the record than randomness.</p>\n<p>I like the word <em>stochastic</em> better, because of its lineage in our language. The first root was <em>stegh</em>, meaning a pointed stake in the Indo-European of 30,000 years ago. <em>Stegh</em> moved into Greek as <em>stokhos</em>, meaning a target for archers, and then later on, in our language, targets being what they are and aiming arrows being as fallible as it is, <em>stokhos</em> was adapted to signify aiming and missing, pure chance, randomness, and thus stochastic. On that philosophical basis, then, I&#8217;m glad to accept all of evolution in a swoop, but I&#8217;m still puzzled by it.</p></blockquote>\n<p>With great subtlety and sensitivity, Thomas then pirouettes to observe that this stochastic miracle of life across time exists <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/01/10/alan-lightman-death/\">only because death too exists</a>. A generation before Richard Dawkins made his poetic point about <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/07/25/richard-dawkins-death/\">the luckiness of death</a> and an epoch after the grief-stricken Darwin, having <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/02/12/annie-darwin/\">lost his most beloved child</a>, found personal solace in the scientific fact that the death of the individual is what fine-tunes evolution to ensure the survival of the species &#8212; &#8220;there is grandeur in this view of life,&#8221; Darwin wrote &#8212; Thomas dismantles the central logical fallacy beneath our species&#8217; fantasies of immortality, be they retro-religious or techno-futuristic. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75660\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/jacobs-dream-by-william-blake-1805_print?sku=s6-22921179p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=680%2C865&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"865\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75660\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=320%2C407&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=600%2C764&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=240%2C305&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=768%2C977&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\"><em>Jacob&#8217;s Dream</em> by William Blake, 1805. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/jacobs-dream-by-william-blake-1805_print?sku=s6-22921179p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/jacobs-dream-by-william-blake-1805_cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, and <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/jacobs-dream-by-william-blake-1805_mask?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With an eye to various speculative proposals &#8212; which have grown all the more various and more unsoundly speculative in the decades since &#8212; about hacking the entropy that frays at all matter in order to attain long-term preservation of information systems, including the information system of us, Thomas considers the inherent syllogism of such hopes: </p>\n<blockquote><p>If it had been arranged that way, we&#8217;d all still be alive forever but, in the nature of things, we would still be those same archaebacteria born 3.7 billion years ago, unable to make molecular errors, deprived of taking chances, and therefore never blundering into brains.</p></blockquote>\n<p>That is, if we could be immortal, <em>we</em> could not exist; if we were already perfect, we could not exist. It is only because we are mortal and imperfect, you and I and Dickinson and Darwin, that the sum of us, the galaxy of humanity drifting through impartial stars, goes on. </p>\n<p>Although he had art on his mind, Van Gogh was contouring a deep scientific truth, a truth both existential and evolutionary, when he observed how <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/11/02/van-gogh-fear-risk/\">inspired mistakes propel us forward</a>.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75729\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-virginia-frances-sterrett-from-old-french-fairy-tales-19206508370_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=680%2C880&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Art by Virginia Frances Sterrett, Old French Fairy Tales, 1920\" width=\"680\" height=\"880\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75729\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=320%2C414&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=600%2C777&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=240%2C311&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=768%2C994&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=1187%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1187w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">One of teenage artist Virginia Frances Sterrett&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/01/27/virginia-frances-sterrett-old-french-fairy-tales/\">century-old illustrations for French fairy tales</a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-virginia-frances-sterrett-from-old-french-fairy-tales-19206508370_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?sort=new?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>With his pliant logic and playful love of the human condition, Thomas considers the reflexive conclusion to which this awareness might lead the inattentive: </p>\n<blockquote><p>Nature is an immense mechanism, operating itself in accordance with the laws of physics. We, and our brains, are working parts of the machinery, having made our appearance here and having our existence because of the operation of those laws, set in place on what we like to see as the pinnacle by the beneficent operation of chance and quantum mechanics. Pure luck, indeterminate and intentionless, all the way.</p></blockquote>\n<p>But this, of course, is Lewis Thomas. And this, therefore, is not a case for vacuous materialism. This is Lewis Thomas, who often makes the deepest point by caricaturing its shallow opposite: </p>\n<blockquote><p>This view takes us a long distance toward understanding our place in nature, but not quite the full distance. We are still stuck with the problem of consciousness, and because of this <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/12/13/stephon-alexander-fear-of-a-black-universe/\">not-quite-settled matter</a>, we are stuck as well with the incessant questions with which our consciousness continues to plague us and disturb our sleep (for which also, by the way, we do not have a good explanation). Questions like: Are we the only creatures on the whole planet with real consciousness? Why is being being; why not nonbeing? Why should there be something, instead of nothing? How do you organize a life, or a society, in accordance with physical laws that forbid purpose, causality, morality, and progress, especially when you have to do so with brains that stand alive with these very notions? Where&#8217;s the fun in it?</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_72735\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"753\" class=\"size-full wp-image-72735\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=240%2C266&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=320%2C354&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=768%2C850&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=600%2C664&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Plate from <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\"><em>An Original Theory or New Hypothesis of the Universe</em></a> by Thomas Wright, 1750. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-from-thomas-wrights-an-original-theory-or-new-hypothesis-of-the-universe-17504457506_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>, as a <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">face mask</a>, and as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In another essay from the book, in a passage from which the entire book borrows its title, Thomas writes at the peak of the Cold War and its menacing specter of nuclear catastrophe, which has since only changed costume as the ecological catastrophe menacing our own time:</p>\n<blockquote><p>This is a very big place, and I do not know how it works, or how I fit in. I am a member of a fragile species, still new to the earth, the youngest creatures of any scale, here only a few moments as evolutionary time is measured, a juvenile species, a child of a species. We are only tentatively set in place, error-prone, at risk of fumbling, in real danger at the moment of leaving behind only a thin layer of our fossils, radioactive at that.</p></blockquote>\n<p>In a passage of extraordinary prescience, precisely in the context of our present ecological precariousness and what its only solution might be, Thomas adds as he considers our place in the family of life:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We are different, to be sure, but not so much because of our brains as because of our discomfiture, mostly with each other. All the other parts of the earth&#8217;s life seem to get along, to fit in with each other, to accommodate, even to concede when the stakes are high. They live off each other, devour each other, scramble for ecological niches, but always within set limits, with something like restraint. It is a rough world, by some of our standards, but not the winner-take-all game that it seemed to us awhile back. If we look over our shoulders as far as we can see, all the way past trillions of other species to those fossil stromatolites built by enormous communities of collaborating microorganisms, we can see no evidence of meanness or vandalism in nature. It is, on balance, an equable, generally amiable place, good-natured as we say.</p>\n<p>We are the anomalies for the moment, the self-conscious children at the edge of the crowd, unsure of our place, tending to grabbiness&#8230; But we are not as bad a lot as some of us say&#8230; At our worst, we may be going through the early stages of a species&#8217; adolescence, and everyone remembers what that is like. Growing up is hard times for an individual but sustained torment for a whole species, especially as brainy and nervous as ours. If we can last it out, get through the phase&#8230;. we might find ourselves off and running again.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75738\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-virginia-frances-sterrett-from-old-french-fairy-tales-1920_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=680%2C883&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Art by Virginia Frances Sterrett, Old French Fairy Tales, 1920\" width=\"680\" height=\"883\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75738\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=320%2C416&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=600%2C780&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=240%2C312&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=768%2C998&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=1182%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1182w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Century-old art by the adolescent <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/01/27/virginia-frances-sterrett-old-french-fairy-tales/\">Virginia Frances Sterrett</a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-virginia-frances-sterrett-from-old-french-fairy-tales-1920_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a> and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/cards?sort=new?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>What might save us from ourselves, Thomas intimates, is not our maturity but our mutuality:</p>\n<blockquote><p>We are more compulsively social, more interdependent and more inextricably attached to each other than any of the celebrated social insects&#8230; One human trait, urging us on by our nature, is the drive to be useful, perhaps the most fundamental of all our biological necessities. We make mistakes with it, get it wrong, confuse it with self-regard, even try to fake it, but it is there in our genes, needing only a better set of definitions for usefulness than we have yet agreed on.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Complement this fragment of <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Fragile-Species-Lewis-Thomas/dp/0684843021/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Fragile Species</em></strong></a> &#8212; which remains one of the finest, most fiercely humanistic and scientifically perspectival books I have ever read &#8212; with philosopher Martha Nussbaum on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2014/03/14/martha-nussbaum-bill-moyers-world-of-ideas/\">how to live with our human fragility</a> and the forgotten visionary William Vogt, writing half a century before his ideas shaped the modern environmental movement, on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/02/18/william-vogt-road-to-survival/\">our interdependence resilience</a>, then revisit Lewis Thomas on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/09/27/lewis-thomas-altruism/\">our wiring for mutuality</a> and his science-rooted existential meditation on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/10/25/lewis-thomas-the-medusa-and-the-snail-self/\">the medusa and the snail</a> &#8212; still the subtlest, sanest thing I have read about the eternal mystery of the self.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/thefragilespecies_lewisthomas.jpg?fit=320%2C482&ssl=1","linkMd5":"15d5f774653d7af25185ea2bb8758114","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn12@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-14-55-144_d868ef32de558eba.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":482,"sourceBytes":38032,"destBytes":38032,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/thefragilespecies_lewisthomas.jpg?fit=320%2C482&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn12@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-14-55-144_d868ef32de558eba.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/darkmatter.jpg?resize=680%2C441&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn28@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-08-172_f4e5aa721bc09c62.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/lewisthomas_galaxy.jpg?resize=595%2C737&ssl=1":null,"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/03/mygod-scaled.jpg?resize=680%2C359&ssl=1":null,"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/williamblake_jacobsdream_small.jpg?resize=680%2C865&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn98@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-08-198_e58fa2e68753e5cc.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett7.jpg?resize=680%2C880&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn6@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-08-131_697cf62ae7fa2f62.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/thomaswright6.jpg?resize=680%2C753&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn65@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-08-699_f65e7634aa3a85e5.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett2.jpg?resize=680%2C883&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn41@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-08-172_bac494c90c1481f7.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245693917},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"Bloom: The Evolution of Life on Earth and the Birth of Ecology (Joan As Police Woman Sings Emily Dickinson)","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75797","description":"<h3>How flowers gave rise to life on Earth and made possible the human consciousness that came to see a world &#8220;thronged only with Music.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p class=\"via\"><em>This is the first of nine installments in the 2021/2022 animated season of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\">The Universe in Verse</a> in collaboration with <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/universe-in-verse/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">On Being</a>, celebrating the wonder of reality through stories of science winged with poetry. See the rest <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/the-universe-in-verse/\">here</a>.</em></p>\n<h5>THE ANIMATED UNIVERSE IN VERSE: CHAPTER ONE</h5>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/animations.jpg?w=532&#038;ssl=1\" /></a>Two hundred million years ago, long before we walked the Earth, it was a world of cold-blooded creatures and dull color &#8212; a kind of terrestrial sea of brown and green. There were plants, but their reproduction was a tenuous game of chance &#8212; they released their pollen into the wind, into the water, against the staggering improbability that it might reach another member of their species. No algorithm, no swipe &#8212; just chance. </p>\n<p>But then, in the Cretaceous period, flowers appeared and carpeted the world with astonishing rapidity &#8212; because, in some poetic sense, they invented love. </p>\n<p>Once there were flowers, there were fruit &#8212; that transcendent alchemy of sunlight into sugar. Once there were fruit, plants could enlist the help of animals in a kind of trade: sweetness for a lift to a mate. Animals savored the sugars in fruit, converted them into energy and proteins, and a new world of warm-blooded mammals came alive. </p>\n<p>Without flowers, there would be no us. </p>\n<p>No poetry.</p>\n<p>No science. </p>\n<p>No music.</p>\n<p>Darwin could not comprehend how flowers could emerge so suddenly and take over so completely. He called it an &#8220;abominable mystery.&#8221; But out of that mystery a new world was born, governed by greater complexity and interdependence and animal desire, with the bloom as its emblem of seduction.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?resize=680%2C383&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75851\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?resize=320%2C180&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?resize=600%2C338&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?resize=240%2C135&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/ernsthaeckel_radiolarians.jpg?resize=768%2C432&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>In 1866, the young German marine biologist <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/03/26/ernst-haeckel-medusae/\">Ernst Haeckel</a> &#8212; whose <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/03/17/ernst-haeckel-radiolaria-film/\">exquisite illustrations</a> of single-celled underwater creatures had enchanted Darwin &#8212; gave that interdependence a name: He called it <em>ecology</em>, from the Greek <em>oikos</em>, or &#8220;house, and <em>logia</em>, or &#8220;the study of,&#8221; denoting the study of the relationship between organisms in the house of life.</p>\n<p>A year earlier, in 1865, a young American poet &#8212; a keen observer of the house of life who made of it a temple of beauty &#8212; composed what is essentially a pre-ecological poem about ecology. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_61497\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?resize=680%2C814&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"814\" class=\"size-full wp-image-61497\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?w=1002&#38;ssl=1 1002w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?resize=240%2C287&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?resize=320%2C383&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?resize=768%2C920&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/emilydickinson.jpg?resize=600%2C719&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Emily Dickinson at seventeen. (Amherst College Archives &#038; Special Collections)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>She had awakened to the interdependent splendor of the natural world as a teenager, when she composed a different kind of ecological poem: In a large album bound in green cloth, she painstakingly pressed, arranged, and labeled in her neat handwriting 424 wildflowers she had gathered from her native New England &#8212; some of them now endangered, some extinct. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=680%2C381&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"381\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75847\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=320%2C179&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=600%2C336&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=240%2C134&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=768%2C430&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>This herbarium &#8212; which survives &#8212; became Emily Dickinson&#8217;s first formal exercise in composition, and although she came to reverence the delicate interleavings of nature in so many of her stunning, spare, strange poems, this one &#8212; the one she wrote in 1865, just before Ernst Haeckel coined <em>ecology</em> &#8212; illuminates and magnifies these relationships through the lens of a single flower and everything that goes into making its bloom &#8212; this emblem of seduction &#8212; possible: the worms in the soil (which Darwin celebrated as the unsung agriculturalists that shaped Earth as we know it), the pollinators in the spring air, all the creatures both competing for resources and symbiotically aiding each other. </p>\n<p>And, suddenly, the flower suddenly emerges not as this pretty object to be admired, but as this ravishing system of aliveness &#8212; a kind of silent symphony of interconnected resilience.</p>\n<p>To bring Emily Dickinson&#8217;s masterpiece to life is a modern-day poet of feeling in music &#8212; also a keen observer of the house of life, also a passionate lover of nature, also an emissary of aliveness through art. </p>\n<p>She is a composer, a multi-instrumentalist classically trained as a violinist, and above all a singer and writer of songs with uncommon sensitivity to the most poetic dimensions of life. </p>\n<p>Here is <a href=\"https://joanaspolicewoman.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Joan As Police Woman</a> with Emily Dickinson and the centuries-old pressed flowers from her actual herbarium. </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Universe in Verse | Part 1: Bloom\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/673019873?h=f009b2400b&#38;dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p><STRONG>BLOOM</STRONG><br />\n<em>by Emily Dickinson</em></p>\n<p>Bloom &#8212; is Result &#8212; to meet a Flower<br />\nAnd casually glance<br />\nWould cause one scarcely to suspect<br />\nThe minor Circumstance<br />\nAssisting in the Bright Affair<br />\nSo intricately done<br />\nThen offered as a Butterfly<br />\nTo the Meridian &#8212;<br />\nTo pack the Bud &#8212; oppose the Worm &#8212;<br />\nObtain its right of Dew &#8212;<br />\nAdjust the Heat &#8212; elude the Wind &#8212;<br />\nEscape the prowling Bee<br />\nGreat Nature not to disappoint<br />\nAwaiting Her that Day &#8212;<br />\nTo be a Flower, is profound<br />\nResponsibility &#8212;\n</p></blockquote>\n<h5>HOW WE MADE IT</h5>\n<p>Every true artist is a miniaturist of grandeur, determined to make every littlest thing the very best it can be &#8212; not out of egoic grandiosity but out of devotion to beauty, devotion paid for with their time and thought, those raw materials of life. When I invited the uncommonly gifted and uncommonly minded <a href=\"https://joanaspolicewoman.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Joan As Police Woman</a> to bring the poem to life in a typical <em>Universe in Verse</em> reading, this true artist instead transformed it into a soulful song &#8212; an homage that would have gladdened the poet, who in her teenage years took regular music lessons and practiced piano for two hours a day, and who grew up to believe that, in its most transcendent stillness, the world is &#8220;thronged only with Music.&#8221;</p>\n<p>From the start, I envisioned using the teenage poet&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2017/05/23/emily-dickinson-herbarium/\">herbarium</a> &#8212; a forgotten treasure at the intersection of art and science, one of my favorite discoveries during the research for <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/12/10/emily-dickinson-love-letters-susan-gilbert/\">the Dickinson chapters of <em>Figuring</em></a> &#8212; as the raw material for the animation art. Having collaborated on a handful of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/04/22/natalie-diaz-lake-loop-ohara-hale-animation/\">previous</a> <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/05/20/anne-sexton-love-poems-song-for-a-lady-ohara-hale/\">animated</a> <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2014/04/28/denise-levertov-92y-ohara-hale/\">poems</a>, I invited <a href=\"https://oharahale.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ohara Hale</a> &#8212; artist, musician, poet, illustrator, animator, maker of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/06/01/be-still-life-ohara-hale/\">nature-reverent children&#8217;s books</a>, choreographer of beauty and feeling across a multitude of art-forms &#8212; to work her visual magic on the poem-song. </p>\n<p>In a small wood cabin at the foot of a Spanish volcano, she set about reanimating &#8212; in both senses of the word &#8212; Emily Dickinson&#8217;s spirit through her herbarium. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?resize=680%2C357&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"357\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75804\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?resize=320%2C168&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?resize=600%2C315&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?resize=240%2C126&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_hand.png?resize=768%2C403&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>Ohara composed all the creatures &#8212; the bee, the caterpillar, the butterflies, the human hand &#8212; from fragments of the poet&#8217;s centuries-old pressed flowers: digitized, restored, retraced by hand, and atomized into new life-forms. Individual petals, leaves, and stamens make the wings, body, and antennae of each butterfly. Layers of petals, sepals, and anthers stripe and behair the body of the bee. A large leaf folds unto itself to shape the hand that wrote this poem and nearly two thousand others &#8212; poems that have long outlived the living matter that felt and composed them, poems that have helped generations live.</p>\n<p>Strewing the animation are words from the poem, hand-lettered by the polymathic <a href=\"http://debbiemillman.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Debbie Millman</a> in a style based on surviving museum samples of Emily Dickinson&#8217;s handwriting from the period in which she composed the herbarium. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?resize=680%2C433&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"433\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75808\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?resize=320%2C204&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?resize=600%2C382&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?resize=240%2C153&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/bloom_elude1.png?resize=768%2C489&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>In a lovely way, the art mirrors the music it serves. Joan&#8217;s composition is itself a time-traveling masterwork of layering: voice upon keys upon strings, feeling-tone upon feeling-tone, classical heritage beneath thoroughly original sensibility &#8212; all of it so consonant with the central poetic image, all of it &#8220;so intricately done,&#8221; all of it a triumph of that &#8220;profound responsibility&#8221; we have to the ecosystem of art and ideas abloom in the spacetime between Emily Dickinson and us. </p>\n<p>It has been an honor to collaborate with these uncommonly gifted women on honoring an uncommonly gifted artistic ancestor and celebrating our common evolutionary ancestry with all life-forms in nature. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. 16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"The Light That Bridges the Dark Expanse Between Lonelinesses: James Baldwin on How Long-Distance Love Illuminates the Power of All Love","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75764","description":"<h3>&#8220;As long as space and time divide you from anyone you love&#8230; love will simply have no choice but to go into battle with space and time and, furthermore, to win.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Richard-Avedon-James-Baldwin-Personal/dp/3836569531/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"424\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?fit=320%2C424&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover with-border alignright size-medium\" alt=\"The Light That Bridges the Dark Expanse Between Lonelinesses: James Baldwin on How Long-Distance Love Illuminates the Power of All Love\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?w=1208&#38;ssl=1 1208w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?resize=240%2C318&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?resize=320%2C424&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?resize=768%2C1018&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/avedonbaldwin_nothingpersonal.jpg?resize=600%2C796&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>The longer I live, the more deeply I learn that love &#8212; whether we call it friendship or family or romance &#8212; is the work of mirroring and magnifying each other&#8217;s light. Gentle work. Steadfast work. Life-saving work in those moments when life and shame and sorrow occlude our own light from our view, but there is still a clear-eyed loving person to beam it back. In our best moments, we are that person for another. </p>\n<p>In learning this afresh &#8212; as we must learn all the great and obvious truths, over and over &#8212; I was reminded of a passage by <strong>James Baldwin</strong> (August 2, 1924&#8211;December 1, 1987) from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Richard-Avedon-James-Baldwin-Personal/dp/3836569531/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Nothing Personal</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/nothing-personal-photos/oclc/9527856&#038;referer=brief_results\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; his 1964 collaboration with the photographer Richard Avedon, his high school classmate and lifelong friend, which contains some of Baldwin&#8217;s least-known yet most intimate writings, including his <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/04/23/james-baldwin-nothing-personal-4-am/\">antidote to dog-hour despair</a> and his <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/05/21/nothing-is-fixed-james-baldwin-morley-music/\">counterforce to entropy</a>. (In the years since I first wrote about this forgotten treasure, it has been unforgotten in a <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Nothing-Personal-James-Baldwin/dp/0807006424/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">new edition</a> by Penguin Random House &#8212; regrettably, without Avedon&#8217;s photographs, razing the spirit of collaboration between friends that occasioned the project in the first place; redemptively, with a foreword by the dazzling <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/07/22/lorraine-hansberry-biography-imani-perry/\">Imani Perry</a>, who considers herself Baldwin&#8217;s &#8220;pupil in the study of humanity&#8221; and who writes splendidly about his enduring gift of reminding us how reading &#8220;allows us to recognize each other&#8221; and &#8220;makes everything seem possible.&#8221;)</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?resize=680%2C425&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"jamesbaldwin\" width=\"680\" height=\"425\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-53759\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?w=1280&#38;ssl=1 1280w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?resize=240%2C150&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?resize=320%2C200&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?resize=768%2C480&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/04/jamesbaldwin.jpg?resize=600%2C375&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">James Baldwin</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the final of the book&#8217;s four essays, Baldwin writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>One discovers the light in darkness, that is what darkness is for; but everything in our lives depends on how we bear the light. It is necessary, while in darkness, to know that there is a light somewhere, to know that in oneself, waiting to be found, there is a light.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This light, Baldwin intimates, is most often and most readily found in love &#8212; that <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/06/06/james-baldwin-giovannis-room-love-choice/\">great and choiceless gift of chance</a>. </p>\n<p>Love becomes a lens on the world, on space and on time &#8212; a pinhole through which a new light enters to project onto <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/03/23/plato-allegory-of-the-cave-ted-ed/\">the cave wall of our consciousness</a> landscapes of intimate importance from territories of being we would have never otherwise known. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75766\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?resize=680%2C566&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"566\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75766\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?w=1179&#38;ssl=1 1179w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?resize=320%2C267&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?resize=600%2C500&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?resize=240%2C200&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/oldfrenchfairytales_sterrett00-1.jpg?resize=768%2C640&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">One of teenage artist Virginia Frances Sterrett&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/01/27/virginia-frances-sterrett-old-french-fairy-tales/\">1920 illustrations for old French fairy tales</a>. (Available as <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/art-by-virginia-frances-sterrett-from-old-french-fairy-tales-19206508378_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>He writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Pretend, for example, that you were born in Chicago and have never had the remotest desire to visit Hong Kong, which is only a name on a map for you; pretend that some convulsion, sometimes called accident, throws you into connection with a man or a woman who lives in Hong Kong; and that you fall in love. Hong Kong will immediately cease to be a name and become the center of your life. And you may never know how many people live in Hong Kong. But you will know that one man or one woman lives there without whom you cannot live. And this is how our lives are changed, and this is how we are redeemed. </p>\n<p>What a journey this life is! Dependent, entirely, on things unseen. If your lover lives in Hong Kong and cannot get to Chicago, it will be necessary for you to go to Hong Kong. Perhaps you will spend your life there, and never see Chicago again. And you will, I assure you, as long as space and time divide you from anyone you love, discover a great deal about shipping routes, airlines, earth quake, famine, disease, and war. And you will always know what time it is in Hong Kong, for you love someone who lives there. And love will simply have no choice but to go into battle with space and time and, furthermore, to win.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_55647\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/total-solar-eclipse-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1878-et5_print#s6-4686076p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?resize=680%2C552&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Total eclipse of the sun, observed July 29, 1878, at Creston, Wyoming Territory\" width=\"680\" height=\"552\" class=\"size-full wp-image-55647\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?w=4885&#38;ssl=1 4885w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?resize=240%2C195&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?resize=320%2C260&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?resize=768%2C624&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?resize=600%2C487&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/07/eclipse.jpg?w=2040&#38;ssl=1 2040w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Total eclipse of the sun by <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2016/07/07/trouvelots-astronomical-drawings/\">Étienne Léopold Trouvelot</a>. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/total-solar-eclipse-by-tienne-lopold-trouvelot-1878-et5_print#s6-4686076p4a1v1?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>, as <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-cards?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stationery cards</a>, and <a href=\"https://society6.com/brainpicker/collection/vintage-science-face-masks?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a face mask</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>A master of metaphor &#8212; that <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/07/07/jane-hirshfield-metaphor/\">handle on the door to new worlds</a> &#8212; Baldwin takes the case of what we call long-distance love and finds in it a miniature of all love. </p>\n<p>All love bridges the immense expanse between lonelinesses, becomes the telescope that brings another life closer and, in consequence, also magnifies the significance of their entire world. </p>\n<p>All love is light&#8217;s battle against the entropy continually inclining spacetime toward nothingness, against the hard fact that you will die, and I will die, and everyone we love will die, and what will survive of us are only <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/03/18/figuring-shoreless-seeds-and-stardust/\">shoreless seeds and stardust</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. flower,&#8221; Emily Dickinson wrote in her <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">pre-ecological poem about ecology</a>, &#8220;is profound Responsibility.&#8221; </p>\n<p>A century later, in one of the most poetic and existentially ravishing children&#8217;s<a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/01/02/the-snail-with-the-right-heart/\">*</a> books of all time, Antoine de Saint-Exupéry made his hero&#8217;s central preoccupation the responsibility for a single flower &#8212; the Little Prince&#8217;s beloved rose: fragile and self-concerned, ferociously hungry for love, capable of such tenderness and such cruelty, so ephemeral and so stubborn, so much a miniature of the contradictory animating forces that make us human. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76022\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_rose.jpg?resize=680%2C553&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"553\" class=\"size-full /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry from the original 1943 edition of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2014/02/03/exupery-little-prince-morgan-drawings/\"><em>The Little Prince</em></a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In the following century, as all stores in Los Angeles were forced to close at the mortal peak of a global pandemic, my photographer friend <a href=\"https://www.elenadorfman.com/floresvitae-gridview\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Elena Dorfman</a> made her way to the city&#8217;s last open flower market, gathered dozens of flowers, and began documenting their slow entropic unblossoming as the days unspooled into weeks &#8212; photographs that became an arresting metaphor for a mortal world suddenly fathoming its fragility and resilience in a new way, suddenly awake to the profound responsibility of staying alive.  </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76018\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/elenadorfman_flowers.jpg?resize=680%2C507&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"507\" class=\"size-full
