class=\"wp-caption-text\">Elena Dorfman. <a href=\"https://www.elenadorfman.com/floresvitae-gridview\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Flores Vitae / Flores Mortes</em></a>. 2020.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>For as long as humans have been alive and awake to our bittersweet cosmic inheritance as transient constellations of atoms capable of transcendent beauty, we have found in flowers <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/02/07/the-moral-of-flowers-rebecca-hey/\">models of moral wisdom</a>, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/06/16/sarah-mapps-douglass-flowers/\">emblems of freedom</a>, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/07/02/perfect-flowers-emily-dickison/\">nonbinary pioneers</a>, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/03/17/sidewalk-flowers/\">portals to paying attention</a>. Over the epochs of time and thought, flowers have <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/03/06/wintering-katherine-may/\">rivaled trees</a> as mirrors for the meaning of our human lives. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_69911\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://society6.com/product/honeysuckle-from-the-moral-of-flowers-1833-by-rebecca-hey_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=680%2C893&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"893\" class=\"size-full wp-image-69911\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=240%2C315&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=320%2C420&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=768%2C1008&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=600%2C788&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Honeysuckle by Rebecca Hey from <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/02/07/the-moral-of-flowers-rebecca-hey/\"><em>The Moral of Flowers</em></a>, 1833. (Available <a href=\"https://society6.com/product/honeysuckle-from-the-moral-of-flowers-1833-by-rebecca-hey_print?curator=brainpicker\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as a print</a>.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>That is what <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/michael-pollan/\">Michael Pollan</a> explores in some lovely passages from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Botany-Desire-Plants-Eye-View-World/dp/0375760393/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>The Botany of Desire</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/botany-of-desire-a-plants-eye-view-of-the-world/oclc/824304662&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; the modern classic that gave us <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/29/michael-pollan-witch-broomstick/\">the radical roots of the flying-witch legend</a> and the story of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/03/broken-tulips/\">how a virus made the world&#8217;s most prized flower</a>. </p>\n<p>In consonance with Borges&#8217;s conviction that <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2016/09/19/a-new-refutation-of-time-borges/\">time is the substance we are made of</a>, Pollan considers time as the tendril by which flowers exert their existential pull on us:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Our experience of flowers is so deeply drenched in our sense of time. Maybe there’s a good reason we find their fleetingness so piercing, can scarcely look at a flower in bloom without thinking ahead, whether in hope or regret. We might share with certain insects a tropism inclining us toward flowers, but presumably insects can look at a blossom without entertaining thoughts of the past and future &#8212; complicated human thoughts that may once have been anything but idle. Flowers have always had important things to teach us about time.</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75847\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=680%2C381&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"381\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75847\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=320%2C179&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=600%2C336&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=240%2C134&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=768%2C430&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Specimens from the teenage Emily Dickinson&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">herbarium</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Time, of course, is itself a creature of paradoxes &#8212; at once the relentless forward momentum of our mortality and <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/08/28/alan-lightman-einsteins-dreams/\">the greatest antidote to the anxiety of aliveness</a>. “When you realize you are mortal you also realize the tremendousness of the future,&#8221; wrote the poet, painter, and philosopher Etel Adnan in her <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/02/06/etel-adnan-journey-to-mount-tamalpais/\">gorgeous meditation on impermanence and transcendence</a>. &#8220;You fall in love with a Time you will never perceive.” </p>\n<p>It may be, Pollan intimates, that flowers betoken precisely this elemental duality and through it cast their enchantment upon us. After contouring <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">their astonishing evolutionary history</a> &#8212; so astonishing that the baffled Darwin called it &#8220;an abominable mystery&#8221; &#8212; he writes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Look into a flower, and what do you see? Into the very heart of nature’s double nature &#8212; that is, the contending energies of creation and dissolution, the spiring toward complex form and the tidal pull away from it. Apollo and Dionysus were names the Greeks gave to these two faces of nature, and nowhere in nature is their contest as plain or as poignant as it is in the beauty of a flower and its rapid passing. There, the achievement of order against all odds and its blithe abandonment. There, the perfection of art and the blind flux of nature. There, somehow, both transcendence <em>and</em> necessity. Could that be it &#8212; right there, in a flower &#8212; the meaning of life?</p></blockquote>\n<p>Meaning, of course, is just what we make of life &#8212; what we make of our mortality <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/02/21/brian-greene-until-the-end-of-time/\">as an inevitability of the universe that made us</a>. “It is the time you have wasted for your rose that makes your rose so important,” the fox says to the Little Price. &#8220;All the stars are a-bloom with flowers,&#8221; the Little Prince says to the pilot before he returns to that fathomless region of spacetime from which he had visited.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_76021\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=680%2C549&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"549\" class=\"size-full wp-image-76021\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=320%2C258&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=600%2C485&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=240%2C194&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=768%2C620&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Antoine de Saint-Exupéry from <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2014/02/03/exupery-little-prince-morgan-drawings/\"><em>The Little Prince</em></a>, 1943.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Complement with Rachel Carson on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/06/07/rachel-carson-the-edge-of-the-sea/\">the ocean as a lens on the meaning of life</a> and Rebecca Solnit on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/09/rebecca-solnit-trees/\">trees and the shape of time</a> &#8212; for any fragment of nature contemplated closely and sensitively enough becomes a lens on human nature and our search for meaning, as Rockwell Kent so keenly felt amid the wild Alaskan solitude, observing that nature is <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/15/rockwell-kent-wilderness/\">&#8220;a kind of living mirror that gives back as its own all and only all that the imagination&#8230; brings to it.&#8221;</a> </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/botanyofdesire.jpg?fit=320%2C493&ssl=1","linkMd5":"8697f90783945ddd29f29d1b3173135a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn23@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-14-57-581_8bc34f315a55a9d3.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":493,"sourceBytes":17482,"destBytes":17482,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/botanyofdesire.jpg?fit=320%2C493&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn23@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-14-57-581_8bc34f315a55a9d3.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_rose.jpg?resize=680%2C553&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn24@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-08-229_d8f8700026900203.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/elenadorfman_flowers.jpg?resize=680%2C507&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn61@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-09-763_1c5d0b8ecc99a3df.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/02/moralofflowers_rebeccahey_honeysuckle1.jpg?resize=680%2C893&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn17@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-08-242_93f610ea568f5e1f.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/emilydickinson_herbarium.jpg?resize=680%2C381&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn41@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-08-505_14751091cf9eee41.webp","https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/thelittleprince_flowers.jpg?resize=680%2C549&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn9@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-09-303_b5db8a9eca02e256.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245693918},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"John Lennon on the Satisfying Difficulty of Excellence and the Vital Role of Invisible Incubation in the Creative Process","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75204","description":"<h3>&#8220;Every song I&#8217;ve ever written has been absolute torture&#8230; except for the ten or so songs the gods give you and that come out of nowhere.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Listening-Interviews-1970-1989-Jonathan-Cott/dp/1517909015/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\"><img width=\"320\" height=\"484\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&#38;ssl=1\" class=\"cover alignright size-medium\" alt=\"John Lennon on the Satisfying Difficulty of Excellence and the Vital Role of Invisible Incubation in the Creative Process\" loading=\"lazy\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?w=397&#38;ssl=1 397w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?resize=320%2C484&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?resize=240%2C363&#38;ssl=1 240w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 320px) 100vw, 320px\" /></a></p><p>“I carry my thoughts about with me for a long time, sometimes a very long time, before I set them down,&#8221; Beethoven, having revolutionized music with his stubborn devotion to making unexampled sound, told a young composer in reflecting on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/11/25/beethoven-on-creativity/\">the role of incubation in his creative process</a>. Two centuries after his death, psychology &#8212; a science not even a glimmer on the horizon of humanity&#8217;s imagination in Beethoven&#8217;s lifetime &#8212; confirmed this intuitive practice, demonstrating that incubation precedes illumination in <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2013/08/28/the-art-of-thought-graham-wallas-stages/\">the five stages of the creative process</a>. </p>\n<p>Beethoven lived before the Age of Celebrity, before this awful contortion of art that bamboozled us into confusing visibility with merit and grandiosity with genius. Amid such confusion, that inner incubus of creativity &#8212; invisible to the outside world, impervious to public appraisal &#8212; is all the more vital, for it is also what enables artists to create rather than cater, to go on making works of truth and beauty answering only to their inner voice and accountable only to their own artistic integrity, rather than producing sellable commodities that fit snugly into some existing market of tastes and expectations. </p>\n<p>That countercultural creative integrity and its relation to private incubation is what <strong>John Lennon</strong> (October 9, 1940&#8211;December 8, 1980) channels in his conversation with Jonathan Cott, included in the altogether shimmering collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Listening-Interviews-1970-1989-Jonathan-Cott/dp/1517909015/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Listening: Interviews, 1970&#8211;1989</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/listening-interviews-1970-1989/oclc/1107060820?referer=br&#038;ht=edition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>).</p>\n<p><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/johnlennon.jpg\" /></p>\n<p>Cott found himself charmed by the way Lennon &#8220;wrote little reminders to himself in the wonderfully absorbed way that a child paints the sun,&#8221; touched by the way this grown man, thrust into a public life and all the cynicism it can catalyze in a person, retained the fundamental childlike sweetness that is always our deepest connection to life &#8212; our own, and the lives of others that compose the shared symphony of aliveness. Cott observes:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Acerbic and skeptical as he could be, John Lennon never lost his sense of compassion.</p></blockquote>\n<p>It is this opinionated, openhearted man of forty that Cott met one December evening in 1980 in Lennon&#8217;s ground-floor apartment at the Dakota &#8212; the iconic twentieth-century castle in Manhattan, in front of which he would be slain by the gruesome antipode of compassion three days later. </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=680%2C533&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"533\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75957\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?w=1520&#38;ssl=1 1520w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=320%2C251&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=600%2C471&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=240%2C188&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=768%2C602&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><br />\nWhat occasioned Cott&#8217;s interview was the release of Lennon&#8217;s collaboration with Yoko Ono, <em>Double Fantasy</em> &#8212; the first record of his in what appeared to the outside world as a five-year creative lull, but was in fact the sort of vital, invisible incubation period out of which so many great works of art are born, the type that artist Rockwell Kent celebrated in the solitary Alaskan wilderness as one of those times in life <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/15/rockwell-kent-wilderness/\">&#8220;when nothing happens &#8212; but in quietness the soul expands.&#8221;</a> Lennon tells Cott:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The illusion that I was cut off from society is a joke. I was just the same as any of the rest of you, I was working from nine to five &#8212; baking bread and changing some nappies and dealing with the baby. People keep asking, &#8220;Why did you go underground, why are you hiding?&#8221; But I wasn&#8217;t hiding&#8230; It was a big event for us to have a baby &#8212; people might forget how hard we tried to have one and how many miscarriages we had and near-death scenes for Yoko&#8230; and we actually had a stillborn child&#8230; We put ourselves in situations that were stressful, but we managed to have the child that we tried to have for ten years, and my God, we weren&#8217;t going to blow it. We didn&#8217;t <em>move</em> for a year, and I took up yoga with the gray-haired lady on TV. [<em>Laughing</em>]</p></blockquote>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75953\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=680%2C455&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"455\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75953\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=320%2C214&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=600%2C402&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=240%2C161&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=768%2C514&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">John Lennon and the convalescing Yoko Ono. (Photograph by <a href=\"https://www.susanwood.com/johnlennon/13\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Susan Wood</a>. Library of Congress.)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In a passage replete with life-tested assurance, echoing Beethoven&#8217;s insight and applicable to anything from new parenthood to pandemic lockdown, Lennon adds:</p>\n<blockquote><p>There&#8217;s a Zen story that Yoko once told me&#8230; A king sent his messenger to an artist to request a painting, he paid the artist money, and the artist said, &#8220;Okay, come back.&#8221; So a year goes by, and the messenger comes back and tells him, &#8220;The king&#8217;s waiting for your painting,&#8221; and the artist says, &#8220;Oh, hold on,&#8221; and whips it right off in front of him and says, &#8220;Here.&#8221; And the messenger says, &#8220;What&#8217;s this? The king paid you twenty thousand bucks for this shit, and you knock it off in five minutes?&#8221; And the painter replies, &#8220;Yeah, but I spent ten years thinking about it.&#8221; And there&#8217;s no way I could have written the <em>Double Fantasy</em> without those five years.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Clad in a torn Jagger T-shirt he had gotten during the Rolling Stones&#8217; 1970 tour, Lennon reflects on a review of his song &#8220;From Me to You&#8221; that dismissed it as &#8220;below par Beatles,&#8221; and considers the odd petty satisfaction critics &#8212; be they paid or self-appointed &#8212; get from chipping at an artist&#8217;s general excellence by magnifying and lambasting small defects in particular works:</p>\n<blockquote><p>Mick&#8217;s put out consistently good work for twenty years, and will they give him a break? Will they ever say, &#8220;Look at him, he&#8217;s Number One, he&#8217;s only thirty-six and he&#8217;s put out a beautiful song, &#8216;Emotional Rescue.'&#8221;&#8230; And God help Bruce Springsteen when they decide he&#8217;s no longer God&#8230; Right now his fans are happy. He&#8217;s told them about being drunk and chasing girls and cars and everything and that&#8217;s about the level they enjoy. But when he gets down to facing his own success and growing older and having to produce it again and again, they&#8217;ll turn on him, and I hope he survives it. All he has to do is look at me or Mick. So it goes up and down, up and down &#8212; of course it does, but what are we, machines?&#8230; When they first criticized &#8220;From Me to You&#8221; as below par Beatles, that&#8217;s when I first realized you&#8217;ve got to keep it up, there&#8217;s some sort of system where you get on the wheel and you&#8217;ve got to keep going around.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Artistic excellence &#8212; as every artist has realized, and some have <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/02/27/harriet-hosmer-figuring/\">enacted and articulated with uncommon clarity</a> &#8212; lies not in running oneself into the ground on this clattering hamster wheel of public approval, but in continually and quietly ascending one&#8217;s own private ladder of creative development. Two centuries after Beethoven told a little girl asking his advice on the creative life that the true artist feels no pride in public admiration but <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2017/05/18/beethoven-emilie-letter/\">&#8220;is sad not to have reached that point to which his better genius only appears as a distant, guiding sun,&#8221;</a> and a century after Georgia O&#8217;Keeffe told the young Sherwood Anderson that <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2014/12/08/georgia-okeeffe-sherwood-anderson-letters/\">&#8220;whether you succeed or not is irrelevant [because] making your unknown known is the important thing &#8212; and keeping the unknown always beyond you,&#8221;</a> Lennon laughs as he tells Cott:</p>\n<blockquote><p>I&#8217;m always complaining about how <em>hard</em> it is to write or how much I <em>suffer</em> when I&#8217;m writing &#8212; that almost every song I&#8217;ve ever written has been absolute torture&#8230; I always think there&#8217;s nothing there, it&#8217;s shit, it&#8217;s no good, it&#8217;s not coming out, this is garbage&#8230; and even if it does come out, I think, &#8220;What the hell is it anyway?&#8221;&#8230; And then I realize that I&#8217;ve been saying that all these years about every session and every song, you know, except for the ten or so songs the gods give you and that come out of nowhere.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Couple this fragment from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Listening-Interviews-1970-1989-Jonathan-Cott/dp/1517909015/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Listening</em></strong></a> with another &#8212; Cott&#8217;s conversation with Bob Dylan about <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/08/27/bob-dylan-jonathan-cott/\">vulnerability, the meaning of integrity, and music as an instrument of truth</a> &#8212; then revisit Rilke on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/06/22/rilke-patience-solitude-art/\">the lonely patience of creative work</a> and Lennon on <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2015/10/09/john-lennon-letters-meditation/\">the value of meditation</a>.</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>. Like? <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/newsletter/\">Sign up.</a></p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 16 Feb 2022 23:18:08 +0000","feedId":17,"bgimg":"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&ssl=1","linkMd5":"7feef1baf18ca7cb0c14a62a4e335365","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn28@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-07-097_cb595626c46ff8cb.webp","destWidth":320,"destHeight":484,"sourceBytes":11892,"destBytes":11892,"author":"Maria Popova","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/08/listening_jonathancott.jpg?fit=320%2C484&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn28@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-07-097_cb595626c46ff8cb.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/10/johnlennon.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn57@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-08-676_b394d5e966b27a93.webp","https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/doublefantasy.jpg?resize=680%2C533&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn35@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-08-986_58d1b9aae95399a8.webp","https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/12/JohnLennon_YokoOno_hospital_SusanWood.jpg?resize=680%2C455&ssl=1":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn28@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-09-378_5a1aaf5a81abc6db.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245693918},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"My God, It’s Full of Stars: Henrietta Leavitt, Edwin Hubble, and Our Human Hunger to Know the Universe (Tracy K. Smith Reads Tracy K. Smith)","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75886","description":"<h3>&#8220;&#8230;so brutal and alive it seemed to comprehend us back.&#8221;</h3>\n<hr>\n<p class=\"via\"><em>This is the second of nine installments in the 2021/2022 animated season of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\">The Universe in Verse</a> in collaboration with <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/universe-in-verse/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">On Being</a>, celebrating the wonder of reality through stories of science winged with poetry. See the rest <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/the-universe-in-verse/\">here</a>.</em></p>\n<h5>THE ANIMATED UNIVERSE IN VERSE: CHAPTER TWO</h5>\n<figure id=\"attachment_64139\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?resize=680%2C468&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"468\" class=\"size-full wp-image-64139\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?resize=240%2C165&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?resize=320%2C220&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?resize=768%2C529&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2018/04/henriettaleavitt_galaxy.jpg?resize=600%2C413&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Henrietta Swan Leavitt</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 1908, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/04/03/the-habits-of-light-anna-leahy-henrietta-leavitt-ann-hamilton/\">Henrietta Swan Leavitt</a> &#8212; one of the women known as the <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2016/12/06/the-glass-universe-dava-sobel/\">Harvard Computers</a>, who changed our understanding of the universe long before they could vote &#8212; was analyzing photographic plates at the Harvard Observatory, singlehandedly measuring and cataloguing more than 2,000 variable stars &#8212; stars that pulsate like lighthouse beacons &#8212; when she began noticing a consistent correlation between their brightness and their blinking pattern. That correlation would allow astronomers to measure their distance for the first time, furnishing the yardstick of the cosmos. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_58835\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Glass-Universe-Harvard-Observatory-Measure/dp/0670016950/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=680%2C680&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"680\" class=\"size-full wp-image-58835\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=240%2C240&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=320%2C320&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=32%2C32&#38;ssl=1 32w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=50%2C50&#38;ssl=1 50w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=64%2C64&#38;ssl=1 64w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=96%2C96&#38;ssl=1 96w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/12/glassplate.jpg?resize=128%2C128&#38;ssl=1 128w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Glass plate of Andromeda from the archives of the &#8220;Harvard Computers.&#8221; (Photograph: Maria Popova)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Meanwhile, a teenage boy in the Midwest was repressing his childhood love of astronomy and beginning his legal studies to fulfill his dying father’s demand for an ordinary, reputable life. Upon his father’s death, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/01/24/the-boy-whose-head-was-filled-with-stars-edwin-hubble/\">Edwin Hubble</a> would unleash his passion for the stars into formal study  and lean on Leavitt’s data to upend millennia of cosmic parochialism, demonstrating two revolutionary facts about the universe: that it is vastly bigger than we thought, and that it is growing bigger by the blink.</p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/01/24/the-boy-whose-head-was-filled-with-stars-edwin-hubble/\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2021/01/hubble_6.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art by Deborah Marcero from <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/01/24/the-boy-whose-head-was-filled-with-stars-edwin-hubble/\"><em>The Boy Whose Head Was Filled with Stars: A Life of Edwin Hubble</em></a> by Isabelle Marinov</figcaption></figure>\n<p>One October evening in 1923, perched at the foot of the world&#8217;s most powerful telescope at Mount Wilson Observatory in California, Hubble took a 45-minute exposure of Andromeda, which was then thought to be one of many spiral nebulae in the Milky Way. The notion of a galaxy &#8212; a gravitationally bound swirl of stars and interstellar gas, dust and dark matter &#8212; did not exist as such. The Milky Way &#8212; a name coined by Chaucer &#8212; was commonly considered an <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/02/16/thomas-wright-original-theory/\">&#8220;island universe&#8221;</a> of stars, beyond the edge of which lay cold dark nothingness. </p>\n<p>When Hubble looked at the photograph the next morning and compared it to previous ones, he (I like to imagine) furrowed his brow, then with a gasp of revelation he (this we know for a fact) crossed out the marking N on the plate, scribbled the letters V A R beneath it, and could not help adding an exclamation point. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75888\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?resize=680%2C844&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"844\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75888\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?w=967&#38;ssl=1 967w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?resize=320%2C397&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?resize=600%2C745&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?resize=240%2C298&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/EdwinHubble_Andromeda_VAR.jpg?resize=768%2C953&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Edwin Hubble&#8217;s 1923 glass plate of Andromeda. (Photograph: Carnegie Observatories)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Hubble had realized that a tiny fleck in Andromeda, previously mistaken for a nova, could not possibly be a nova, given its blinking pattern across the different photographs. It was a variable star &#8212; which, given Henrietta Leavitt&#8217;s discovery, could only be so if the tiny fleck was very far away, farther than the edge of the Milky Way. </p>\n<p>Andromeda was not a nebula in our own galaxy but a separate galaxy, out there in the cold dark nothingness. </p>\n<p>Suddenly, the universe was a garden blooming with galaxies, with ours but a single <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">bloom</a>. </p>\n<p>That same year, in another country suspended between two World Wars, another young scientist named Hermann Oberth was polishing the final physics on a daring idea: to subvert a deadly military technology with roots in medieval China and rocket-launch an enormous telescope into Earth orbit &#8212; closer to the stars, bypassing the atmosphere that occludes our terrestrial instruments. </p>\n<p>It would take two generations of scientists to make that telescope a reality &#8212; a shimmering poem of metal, physics, and perseverance, bearing Hubble&#8217;s name.</p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_75889\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?resize=680%2C449&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"449\" class=\"size-full wp-image-75889\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?w=1100&#38;ssl=1 1100w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?resize=320%2C211&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?resize=600%2C397&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?resize=240%2C159&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/HubbleSpaceTelescope.jpg?resize=768%2C508&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">The Hubble Space Telescope. (Photograph: NASA)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>But when the Hubble Space Telescope finally launched 1990, hungry to capture the most intimate images of the cosmos humanity had yet seen, humanity had crept into the instrument&#8217;s exquisite precision &#8212; its main mirror had been ground into the wrong spherical shape, warping its colossal eye.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Life-Mars-Tracy-K-Smith/dp/1555975844/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/lifeonmars_tracyksmith.jpg\" /></a>Up the coast from Mount Wilson Observatory, a teenage girl watched her father &#8212; who had worked on the Hubble as one of NASA&#8217;s first black engineers &#8212; come home brokenhearted. He didn&#8217;t know that his observant daughter would become Poet Laureate of his country and would come to commemorate him in the tenderest tribute an artist-daughter has ever made for a scientist-father. That tribute &#8212; the splendid poetry collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Life-Mars-Tracy-K-Smith/dp/1555975844/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Life on Mars</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"http://www.worldcat.org/title/life-on-mars-poems/oclc/794038356&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>) &#8212; earned Tracy K. Smith the Pulitzer Prize the year the Hubble&#8217;s corrected optics captured the revolutionary Ultra Deep Field image of the observable universe, revealing what neither Henrietta Leavitt nor Edwin Hubble could have imagined &#8212; that there isn&#8217;t just one other galaxy besides our own, or just a handful more, but at least 100 billion, each containing at least 100 billion stars. </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Universe in Verse | Part 2: My God, It&#38;rsquo;s Full of Stars\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/676129501?h=004ba6708a&#38;dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"359\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>MY GOD, IT&#8217;S FULL OF STARS (PART 5)</strong><br />\n<em>by Tracy K. Smith</em></p>\n<p>When my father worked on the Hubble Telescope, he said<br />\nThey operated like surgeons: scrubbed and sheathed<br />\nIn papery green, the room a clean cold, a bright white.</p>\n<p>He&#8217;d read Larry Niven at home, and drink scotch on the rocks,<br />\nHis eyes exhausted and pink. These were the Reagan years,<br />\nWhen we lived with our finger on The Button and struggled</p>\n<p>To view our enemies as children. My father spent whole seasons<br />\nBowing before the oracle-eye, hungry for what it would find.<br />\nHis face lit up whenever anyone asked, and his arms would rise</p>\n<p>As if he were weightless, perfectly at ease in the never-ending<br />\nNight of space. On the ground, we tied postcards to balloons<br />\nFor peace. Prince Charles married Lady Di. Rock Hudson died.</p>\n<p>We learned new words for things. The decade changed.</p>\n<p>The first few pictures came back blurred, and I felt ashamed<br />\nFor all the cheerful engineers, my father and his tribe. The second time,<br />\nThe optics jibed. We saw to the edge of all there is &#8212; </p>\n<p>So brutal and alive it seemed to comprehend us back.</p></blockquote>\n<h5>THE MAKING</h5>\n<p>Every poet is a miniaturist of meaning, building cathedrals of beauty and truth with the smallest particles of language. It is with a poet&#8217;s mindset that Brazilian graphic artist and animation director <a href=\"https://danielbruson.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Daniel Bruson</a> approached his contribution to <em>The Universe in Verse</em>. (Special thanks to <em>On Being</em> creative director Erin Colasacco for bringing Daniel into the project and for working with him and with composer <a href=\"https://www.floatingfast.com\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Gautam Srikishan</a> on making this symphonic cinepoem come alive.)</p>\n<p>After I relayed to Daniel why I had chosen this particular poem (which Tracy <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2017/05/12/tracy-k-smith-life-on-mars/\">read at the inaugural <em>Universe in Verse</em></a> in 2017) to illustrate the larger story of our search for cosmic truth &#8212; a search both made possible and made imperfect by our humanity &#8212; he grasped the nested layers of meaning with uncommon sensitivity, mirroring back his interpretation:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The Hubble tries to see or make sense of the Universe, the father tries to understand the Hubble, the daughter tries to make sense of the father, the decade, the world, and the poet tries to put this whole into perspective. All these efforts have to face problems of scale or distortion: something too big or small, too close or too distant, too dark or too familiar. Not to mention the original problem with the Hubble mirror.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This cascade of distortion sparked the idea &#8220;to use optics as a metaphor, to seek for these imperfect, unresolved and elusive, but also suggestive and alive images.&#8221; </p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=680%2C359&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"359\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75893\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?w=2560&#38;ssl=1 2560w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=320%2C169&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=600%2C316&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=240%2C127&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=768%2C405&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=1536%2C810&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?resize=2048%2C1080&#38;ssl=1 2048w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars1-scaled.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>Daniel set about creating his deliberately blurry cosmic animations frame by frame, painting each tiny detail onto a glass plate with nail polish, oil paint, glitter, acrylic, and other materials he mixed, scrubbed, smudged, and swirled with brushes and cotton swabs beneath the lens of a camera capturing the process of creation and destruction.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=680%2C907&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"907\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75890\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=320%2C427&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=600%2C800&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=240%2C320&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=768%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson1.jpg?resize=1152%2C1536&#38;ssl=1 1152w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?resize=680%2C359&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"359\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75895\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?resize=320%2C169&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?resize=600%2C317&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?resize=240%2C127&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars2.jpg?resize=768%2C405&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>He magnified the optical enchantment by filming the vignettes through upside-down drinking glasses of various shapes and thicknesses.</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson3.jpg?resize=680%2C648&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"648\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75891\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson3.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson3.jpg?resize=768%2C732&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?resize=680%2C482&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"482\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75892\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?resize=320%2C227&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?resize=600%2C425&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?resize=240%2C170&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/universeinverse_danielburson2.jpg?resize=768%2C544&#38;ssl=1 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>In a crowning feat of ingenuity &#8212; itself a miniature masterpiece of engineering and composition &#8212; he built a tiny model of the Hubble out of cardboard, paper, and aluminum foil, dismantled it frame by frame, filmed the destruction, then reversed the footage to create the building effect. (I am reminded here of Bertrand Russell&#8217;s astute observation, made shortly after Edwin Hubble took his historic glass plate of Andromeda, that <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2013/02/21/education-and-the-good-life-bertrand-russell/\">&#8220;construction and destruction alike satisfy the will to power, but construction is more difficult as a rule, and therefore gives more satisfaction to the person who can achieve it&#8221;</a> &#8212; a truth as true of the universe itself, with its elemental triumph of something over nothing, as it is of the human endeavor to know it by building optical prosthesis of our curiosity.)</p>\n<p><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=680%2C359&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"359\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-75894\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?w=2560&#38;ssl=1 2560w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=320%2C169&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=600%2C316&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=240%2C127&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=768%2C405&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=1536%2C810&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?resize=2048%2C1080&#38;ssl=1 2048w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/mygoditsfullofstars3-scaled.jpg?w=1360&#38;ssl=1 1360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></p>\n<p>Something about Daniel&#8217;s process &#8212; the exquisite craftsmanship, the passionate patience, the tiny scale on which he made such beauty and grandeur of feeling &#8212; calls to mind Emily Dickinson and her miniature cherrywood writing desk, on the seventeen square inches of which she conjured up such cosmoses of truth, among them the poem illustrating <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">Chapter One</a> of this series. </p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. 16:14:53","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:14:53","title":"Achieving Perspective: Trailblazing Astronomer Maria Mitchell and the Poetry of the Cosmic Perspective (David Byrne Reads Pattiann Rogers)","link":"https://www.themarginalian.org/?p=75965","description":"<h3>&#8220;Mingle the starlight with your lives, and you won&#8217;t be fretted by trifles.&#8221; </h3>\n<hr>\n<p class=\"via\"><em>This is the third of nine installments in the 2021/2022 animated season of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\">The Universe in Verse</a> in collaboration with <a href=\"https://onbeing.org/universe-in-verse/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">On Being</a>, celebrating the wonder of reality through stories of science winged with poetry. See the rest <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/the-universe-in-verse/\">here</a>.</em></p>\n<h5>THE ANIMATED UNIVERSE IN VERSE: CHAPTER THREE</h5>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/the-universe-in-verse/\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/animations.jpg?w=532&#038;ssl=1\" /></a>To be human is to live suspended between the scale of glow-worms and the scale of galaxies, to live with our creaturely limitations without being doomed by them &#8212; we have, after all, transcended them to unravel the molecular mystery of the double helix and compose the <em>Benedictus</em> and land a mechanical prosthesis of our curiosity on Mars. We have dreamt these things possible, then made them real &#8212; proof that we are a species of limitless imagination along the forward vector of our dreams. But we are also a species continually blinkered &#8212; sometimes touchingly, sometimes tragically &#8212; by our own delusions about the totality around us. Our greatest limitation is not that of imagination but that of perspective &#8212; our lens is too easily contracted by the fleeting urgencies of the present, too easily blurred by the hopes and fears of our human lives.</p>\n<p>Two centuries ago, <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/tag/maria-mitchell/\">Maria Mitchell</a> &#8212; a key figure in <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2018/11/01/figuring/\"><em>Figuring</em></a> &#8212; understood this with uncommon poetry of perspective. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_61912\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?resize=680%2C797&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"797\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-61917\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?resize=240%2C281&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?resize=320%2C375&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?resize=768%2C900&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/10/mitchell_telescope-1.jpg?resize=600%2C703&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Portrait of Maria Mitchell, 1840s. (Maria Mitchell Museum. Photograph: Maria Popova)</figcaption></figure>\n<p>America&#8217;s first professional female astronomer, she was also the first woman employed by the federal government for a &#8220;specialized non-domestic skill.&#8221; After discovering <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2013/10/01/october-1-1847-miss-mitchells-comet/\">her famous comet</a>, she was hired as &#8220;computer of Venus,&#8221; performing complex mathematical calculations to help sailors navigate the globe &#8212; a one-woman global positioning system a century and a half before Einstein&#8217;s theory of relativity made GPS possible. </p>\n<p>When Maria Mitchell began teaching at Vassar College as the only woman on the faculty, the college handbook mandated that neither she nor her female students were allowed outside after nightfall &#8212; a somewhat problematic dictum, given she was hired to teach astronomy. She overturned the handbook and overwrote the curriculum, creating the country&#8217;s most ambitious science syllabus, soon copied by other universities &#8212; including the all-male Harvard, which had long dropped its higher mathematics requirement past the freshman year. </p>\n<p>Maria Mitchell&#8217;s students went on to become the world&#8217;s first class with academic training in what we now call astrophysics. They happened to all be women. </p>\n<figure id=\"attachment_59515\"  class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/Mitchell-Letters-Journals-Classic-Reprint/dp/1451018460/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?resize=680%2C413&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"413\" class=\"size-full wp-image-59515\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?w=1145&#38;ssl=1 1145w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?resize=240%2C146&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?resize=320%2C194&#38;ssl=1 320w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?resize=768%2C466&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/mariamitchell_telescope.jpg?resize=600%2C364&#38;ssl=1 600w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Maria Mitchell, standing at telescope, with her students at Vassar</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Science was one of Maria Mitchell&#8217;s two great passions. The other was poetry. </p>\n<p>At her regular &#8220;dome parties&#8221; inside the Vassar College Observatory, which was also her home, students and occasional esteemed guests &#8212; Julia Ward Howe among them &#8212; gathered to play a game of writing extemporaneous verses about astronomy on scraps of used paper: sonnets to the stars, composed on the back of class notes and calculations.</p>\n<p>Mitchell taught astronomy until the very end of her long life, when she confided in one of her students that she would rather have written a great poem than discovered a great comet. But scientific discovery is what gave her the visibility to blaze the way for women in science and enchant generations of lay people the poetry of <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2017/12/21/reflection/\">the cosmic perspective</a>. </p>\n<figure  class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/10/01/what-miss-mitchell-saw/\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/whatmissmitchellsaw0.jpg\" /></a><figcaption class=\"wp-caption-text\">Art from <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2019/10/01/what-miss-mitchell-saw/\"><em>What Miss Mitchell Saw</em></a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>It was this living example that became Maria Mitchell&#8217;s great poem, composed in the language of being &#8212; as any life of passion and purpose ultimately becomes. </p>\n<p>&#8220;Mingle the starlight with your lives,&#8221; she often told her students, &#8220;and you won&#8217;t be fretted by trifles.&#8221; </p>\n<p>And yet here we are, our transient lives constantly fretted by trifles as we live them out in the sliver of spacetime allotted us by chance. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Firekeeper-Selected-Poems-Pattiann-Rogers/dp/1571314210/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><img class=\"cover\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/www.themarginalian.org/wp-content/uploads/2022/02/firekeeper_pattiannrogers.jpg?w=680&#038;ssl=1\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></a>A century after Maria Mitchell returned her borrowed stardust to the universe that made it, the poet Pattiann Rogers extended a kindred invitation to perspective, untrifling the tender moments that make a life worth living. </p>\n<p>Published in her collection <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Firekeeper-Selected-Poems-Pattiann-Rogers/dp/1571314210/?tag=braipick-20\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong><em>Firekeeper</em></strong></a> (<a href=\"https://www.worldcat.org/title/firekeeper-selected-poems/oclc/1154359922&#038;referer=brief_results\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>public library</em></a>), it is read for us here by the <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/05/14/one-fine-day-david-byrne-brooklyn-youth-chorus-national-sawdust/\">ever-optimistic</a> David Byrne, with original art by his <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/06/22/maira-kalman-darling-baby/\">ever-perspectival</a> <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2020/11/29/american-utopia-maira-kalman-david-byrne/\">longtime collaborator</a> Maira Kalman and original music by the symphonic-spirited <a href=\"https://www.patreon.com/jherekbischoff\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Jherek Bischoff</a>. </p>\n<p><iframe loading=\"lazy\" title=\"The Universe in Verse | Part 3: Achieving Perspective\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/679248186?h=b24c7f236e&#38;dnt=1&#38;app_id=122963\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p><strong>ACHIEVING PERSPECTIVE</strong><br />\n<em>by Pattiann Rogers</em></p>\n<p>Straight up away from this road,<br />\nAway from the fitted particles of frost<br />\nCoating the hull of each chick pea,<br />\nAnd the stiff archer bug making its way<br />\nIn the morning dark, toe hair by toe hair,<br />\nUp the stem of the trillium,<br />\nStraight up through the sky above this road right now,<br />\nThe galaxies of the Cygnus A cluster<br />\nAre colliding with each other in a massive swarm<br />\nOf interpenetrating and exploding catastrophes.<br />\nI try to remember that.</p>\n<p>And even in the gold and purple pretense<br />\nOf evening, I make myself remember<br />\nThat it would take 40,000 years full of gathering<br />\nInto leaf and dropping, full of pulp splitting<br />\nAnd the hard wrinkling of seed, of the rising up<br />\nOf wood fibers and the disintegration of forests,<br />\nOf this lake disappearing completely in the bodies<br />\nOf toad slush and duckweed rock,<br />\n40,000 years and the fastest thing we own,<br />\nTo reach the one star nearest to us.</p>\n<p>And when you speak to me like this,<br />\nI try to remember that the wood and cement walls<br />\nOf this room are being swept away now,<br />\nMolecule by molecule, in a slow and steady wind,<br />\nAnd nothing at all separates our bodies<br />\nFrom the vast emptiness expanding, and I know<br />\nWe are sitting in our chairs<br />\nDiscoursing in the middle of the blackness of space.<br />\nAnd when you look at me<br />\nI try to recall that at this moment<br />\nSomewhere millions of miles beyond the dimness<br />\nOf the sun, the comet Biela, speeding<br />\nIn its rocks and ices, is just beginning to enter<br />\nThe widest arc of its elliptical turn.</p></blockquote>\n<p class=\"via\">Previously on <em>The Universe in Verse</em>: <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/04/universe-in-verse-animated-episode-1/\">Chapter 1</a> (the evolution of flowers and the birth of ecology, with Emily Dickinson); <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2022/02/11/universe-in-verse-animated-hubble/\">Chapter 2</a> (Henrietta Leavitt, Edwin Hubble, and the age of space telescopes, with Tracy K. Smith).</p>\n<hr /><h3>donating = loving</h3><p class=\"flipboard-keep\">For a decade and half, I have been spending hundreds of hours and thousands of dollars each month composing <em>The Marginalian</em> (which <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/2021/10/22/brain-pickings-becoming-the-marginalian/\">bore the unbearable name <em>Brain Pickings</em></a> for its first fifteen years). It has remained free and ad-free and alive thanks to patronage from readers. I have no staff, no interns, no assistant — a thoroughly one-woman labor of love that is also my life and my livelihood. If this labor makes your own life more livable in any way, please consider lending a helping hand with a <a href=\"https://www.themarginalian.org/donate/\">donation</a>. Your support makes all the difference.</p>\n\n<hr />\n\n<h3>newsletter</h3>\n<p><em>The Marginalian</em> has a free weekly newsletter. It comes out on Sundays and offers the week’s most inspiring reading. Here’s <a href=\"https://mailchi.mp/brainpickings/janna-levin-rebecca-elson-anne-lamott-james-gleick\">what to expect</a>.
